         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="smtd202301277-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/ef392729-ff14-4306-94bf-373e8a14cc04/smtd202301277-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/ef392729-ff14-4306-94bf-373e8a14cc04/smtd202301277-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/4c129fc2-d07d-46c1-8c92-b4457e52545d/smtd202301277-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/ef392729-ff14-4306-94bf-373e8a14cc04/smtd202301277-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smtd202301277-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmtd.202301277" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Electrochemical performance at 25&nbsp;°C. a) CV curves of NVPF@rGO/CNT at different scan rates from 0.1 to 2&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>, b) CV curves of NVPF@rGO/CNT, NVPF@rGO, and NVPF at 2&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>, c) b values at different potentials, d) Nyquist plots, insets are corresponding fitted equivalent circuits, e) the relationship between Z’ and ω<sup>−1/2</sup>, and&nbsp;f) chematic diagram of the electron transmission path of NVPF@rGO/CNT.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <div class="paragraph-element">The CV curves of the NVPF@rGO/CNT electrode exhibit near-perfect symmetry, indicating extraordinary electrochemical reversibility. Redox peaks exhibit minimal shifts as scan rates increase, indicating rapid electrochemical kinetics of the NVPF@rGO/CNT electrode. More remarkably, the potential gap (∆<i>V</i> and ∆<i>V’</i> values), standing for polarization depth,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smtd202301277-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smtd202301277-bib-0024_R_d41595900e1223" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - J. Am. Chem. Soc.">24</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> is estimated as ∆<i>V</i> = 105.6&nbsp;mV and ∆<i>V’</i> = 99.3&nbsp;mV at 2&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smtd202301277-fig-0005">5b</a>). By contrast, ∆<i>V</i> values (∆<i>V’</i>) of NVPF@rGO and NVPF are even larger and calculated as 163 (155.2) mV and 122.4 (131) mV at 2&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup> respectively, which absolutely signifies faster Na<sup>+</sup> redox dynamics of NVPF@rGO/CNT cathode. Typically, the scan rate (<i>v</i>) and peak current (<i>i</i><sub>p</sub>) follow the equations given below<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smtd202301277-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smtd202301277-bib-0025_R_d41595900e1252" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Nat. Commun. Battery Energy">25</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup>:

            <div class="inline-equation" id="smtd202301277-disp-0003"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                  <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/c9e71995-fbfb-44bc-accb-bd04f599c7fe/smtd202301277-math-0003.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:23669608:media:smtd202301277:smtd202301277-math-0003" display="block" location="graphic/smtd202301277-math-0003.png">
                     <semantics>
                        <mrow>
                           <msub>
                              <mi>i</mi>
                              <mi mathvariant="normal">p</mi>
                           </msub>
                           <mo linebreak="badbreak">=</mo>
                           <mi>a</mi>
                           <msup>
                              <mi>v</mi>
                              <mi mathvariant="normal">b</mi>
                           </msup>
                        </mrow>
                        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}{i}_{\mathrm{p}} = a{v}^{\mathrm{b}}\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                     </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(3)</span></div>
            <div class="inline-equation" id="smtd202301277-disp-0004"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                  <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/aae52d22-1282-4c1c-bf70-8435e9b7f377/smtd202301277-math-0004.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:23669608:media:smtd202301277:smtd202301277-math-0004" display="block" location="graphic/smtd202301277-math-0004.png">
                     <semantics>
                        <mrow>
                           <mi>log</mi>
                           <mfenced close=")" open="(" separators="">
                              <msub>
                                 <mi>i</mi>
                                 <mi mathvariant="normal">p</mi>
                              </msub>
                           </mfenced>
                           <mo linebreak="badbreak">=</mo>
                           <mi>b</mi>
                           <mi>log</mi>
                           <mfenced close=")" open="(">
                              <mi>v</mi>
                           </mfenced>
                           <mo linebreak="goodbreak">+</mo>
                           <mi>log</mi>
                           <mfenced close=")" open="(">
                              <mi>a</mi>
                           </mfenced>
                        </mrow>
                        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}\log \left( {{i}_{\mathrm{p}}} \right) = b\log \left( v \right) + \log \left( a \right)\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                     </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(4)</span></div>where a and b are adjustable parameters. By capturing the peak currents (<i>i</i><sub>p</sub>) of the cathodic (O, O’) and anodic peaks (R, R’) at every scanning rate (<i>v</i>), plotted log(<i>i</i><sub>p</sub>) versus log(<i>v</i>) plots and their corresponding fitted linear correlations as shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11</a> (Supporting Information). As known by all, when the value of b approaches 1, it is a surface capacitance dominant process, and when the value of b approaches 0.5, it is a diffusion-controlled process. For a more intuitive comparison, show all the b-values in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smtd202301277-fig-0005">5c</a>. The b-values of R1, O1, R1’, and O1’ are calculated to be 0.883, 0.881, 0.927, and 0.929 for NVPF@rGO/CNT respectively. Notably, all redox peaks for the NVPF@rGO/CNT have higher b-values than those for the NVPF@rGO and NVPF electrodes, indicating that the NVPF@rGO/CNT electrode has faster electrochemical reaction kinetics. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smtd202301277-fig-0005">5d</a> shows Nyquist plots. The semicircle in the high-frequency range corresponds to the charge transfer resistance (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>) at the interfaces between the electrolyte and electrode. The leaning lines in the low-frequency scope refer to Warburg resistance (<i>Z</i><sub>W</sub>) of Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion in the active material host.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smtd202301277-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smtd202301277-bib-0026_R_d41595900e1332" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - J. Mater. Chem. A Nano Energy">26</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The NVPF@rGO/CNT electrode exhibits the lowest <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> of only 2.1 Ω, which is on account of the 3D conductive network integration by rGO and CNT accelerating the transmission of electrons and enhancing the conductivity of the electrode. Compared to NVPF@rGO electrodes, NVPF@rGO/CNT electrodes have more conductive paths in their 3D conductive network, which can effectively enhance electronic transfer between NVPF nanoparticles (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smtd202301277-fig-0005">5f</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12</a>, Supporting Information). Additionally, the Na<sup>+</sup> ion diffusion coefficient (D<sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup>) can be approximated through the low-frequency plots based on the equations<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smtd202301277-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smtd202301277-bib-0027_R_d41595900e1352" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Adv. Energy Mater.">27</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup>:

            <div class="inline-equation" id="smtd202301277-disp-0005"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                  <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/e86ce302-2bca-4981-82d7-093674b0db80/smtd202301277-math-0005.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:23669608:media:smtd202301277:smtd202301277-math-0005" display="block" location="graphic/smtd202301277-math-0005.png">
                     <semantics>
                        <mrow>
                           <msub>
                              <mi>D</mi>
                              <mrow>
                                 <mi>N</mi>
                                 <msup>
                                    <mi>a</mi>
                                    <mo>+</mo>
                                 </msup>
                              </mrow>
                           </msub>
                           <mo linebreak="badbreak">=</mo>
                           <msup>
                              <mi>R</mi>
                              <mn>2</mn>
                           </msup>
                           <mspace width="0.33em"></mspace>
                           <msup>
                              <mi>T</mi>
                              <mn>2</mn>
                           </msup>
                           <mo>/</mo>
                           <mfenced close=")" open="(" separators="">
                              <mrow>
                                 <mn>2</mn>
                                 <msup>
                                    <mi>A</mi>
                                    <mn>2</mn>
                                 </msup>
                                 <msup>
                                    <mi>n</mi>
                                    <mn>4</mn>
                                 </msup>
                                 <msup>
                                    <mi>F</mi>
                                    <mn>4</mn>
                                 </msup>
                                 <msup>
                                    <mi>C</mi>
                                    <mn>2</mn>
                                 </msup>
                                 <msup>
                                    <mi>σ</mi>
                                    <mn>2</mn>
                                 </msup>
                              </mrow>
                           </mfenced>
                        </mrow>
                        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}{D}_{N{a}^ + } = {R}^2\ {T}^2/\left( {2{A}^2{n}^4{F}^4{C}^2{\sigma }^2} \right)\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                     </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(5)</span></div>
            <div class="inline-equation" id="smtd202301277-disp-0006"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                  <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/f6cb0408-f44f-46bd-b1d8-af3ca636d2e7/smtd202301277-math-0006.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:23669608:media:smtd202301277:smtd202301277-math-0006" display="block" location="graphic/smtd202301277-math-0006.png">
                     <semantics>
                        <mrow>
                           <msup>
                              <mi>Z</mi>
                              <mo>′</mo>
                           </msup>
                           <mo linebreak="badbreak">=</mo>
                           <msub>
                              <mi>R</mi>
                              <mrow>
                                 <mi>c</mi>
                                 <mi>t</mi>
                              </mrow>
                           </msub>
                           <mspace width="0.33em"></mspace>
                           <mo linebreak="goodbreak">+</mo>
                           <mi>σ</mi>
                           <msup>
                              <mi>ω</mi>
                              <mrow>
                                 <mo>−</mo>
                                 <mn>1</mn>
                                 <mo>/</mo>
                                 <mn>2</mn>
                              </mrow>
                           </msup>
                        </mrow>
                        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}Z^{\prime} = {R}_{ct}\ + \sigma {\omega }^{ - 1/2}\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                     </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(6)</span></div>where <i>C</i>, <i>F</i>, <i>n</i>, <i>A</i>, <i>T</i>, and <i>R</i> correspond to the concentration of ions, the Faraday constant, the number of electrons in the charged state, efficient work area, temperature, and the gas constant, respectively. Based on the above formula, there is an inverse relationship between Warburg coefficient (<i>σ</i>) and D<sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> values. As σ decreases, D<sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> increases, resulting in a faster Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion rate. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smtd202301277-fig-0005">5e</a> demonstrates the Z’ versus ω<sup>−1/2</sup> plots, where the σ value is determined from its slope. The NVPF@rGO/CNT composite shows a considerably lower <i>σ</i> value compared to NVPF@rGO and NVPF, suggesting a higher Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics for NVPF@rGO/CNT. The GITT technique is used to measure the electrochemical storage dynamics of Na<sup>+</sup>. GITT curves of the NVPF@rGO/CNT, NVPF@rGO, and NVPF are portrayed in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#smtd202301277-fig-0006">6a–c</a>. Based on the GITT profiles, the D<sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> values are calculated and summarized during the charging/discharging processes (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smtd202301277-fig-0006">6d–f</a>). Typically, the D<sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> value of NVPF@rGO/CNT ranges from 5&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−10</sup> to 8&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−10</sup>, which is higher than that of NVPF@rGO (from 4&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−10</sup> to 7&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−10</sup>) and NVPF (from 10<sup>−11</sup> to 3&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−10</sup>), show faster Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics in NVPF@rGO/CNT. Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13</a> (Supporting Information) presents the in-situ EIS spectrum change of the NVPF@rGO/CNT of the first cycle. At the open circuit voltage (OCV), the ohmic resistance (<i>R</i><sub>s</sub>) and the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> is 5.75 and 2.1 Ω, respectively. During the charging and discharging process, the <i>R</i><sub>s</sub> and <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> values of NVPF@rGO/CNT remain basically unchanged. After discharging from 4.3 to 2.5&nbsp;V, the <i>R</i><sub>s</sub> and <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> are 6 and 2.3 Ω respectively, indicating the outstanding structural stability and electrochemical reversibility of NVPF@rGO/CNT.</div>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="smtd202301277-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/0fadafcb-b6d6-4433-9863-158ced0bc583/smtd202301277-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/0fadafcb-b6d6-4433-9863-158ced0bc583/smtd202301277-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/2861674f-dcce-4dc6-b8ef-3cf38b033794/smtd202301277-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/0fadafcb-b6d6-4433-9863-158ced0bc583/smtd202301277-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smtd202301277-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmtd.202301277" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">GITT profiles and Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient. a,d) NVPF@rGO/CNT, b,e) NVPF@rGO, and c,f) NVPF.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The structural evolution of the NVPF@rGO/CNT cathode during the first cycle was studied by ex situ XRD technique (<b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#smtd202301277-fig-0007">7a</a>). No new diffraction peaks were observed during the process of sodium ion insertion/extraction. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smtd202301277-fig-0007">7b</a> shows a close-up of some diffraction peaks. Overall, in the XRD profiles, the (1 1 1), (0 0 2), (2 2 0), (1 1 3), and (2 2 2) diffraction peaks of NVPF@rGO/CNT (2<i>θ</i> = 16.17°, 16.63°, 27.9°, 28.73°, and 32.67°) shift to higher angles (2<i>θ</i> = 16.2°, 16.71°, 27.98°, 28.85°, and 32.76°) during dissociation process from OCV to 4.3&nbsp;V, indicating the cell volume shrinkage. Upon the ensuing sodiation procedure from 4.3 to 2.5&nbsp;V, these diffraction peaks can highly reverse return to the original angles, indicating the fully reversible Na<sup>+</sup> extraction/insertion processes. It is worth noting that the deflection angle of the diffraction peak is extremely small, and the calculated volume change of the NVPF@rGO/CNT is only 0.4%, which demonstrates the zero-strain characteristic. The NVPF@rGO/CNT cathode exhibits a significantly lower volume variability compared to other widely studied cathodes with NASICON structure and layered oxides. (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smtd202301277-fig-0007">7c</a>; Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="smtd202301277-fig-0007"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/f39fbaef-7495-46df-9a7e-edce472630a4/smtd202301277-fig-0007-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/f39fbaef-7495-46df-9a7e-edce472630a4/smtd202301277-fig-0007-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/ac23343c-1d49-48b6-8434-ce49feb825fb/smtd202301277-fig-0007-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/f39fbaef-7495-46df-9a7e-edce472630a4/smtd202301277-fig-0007-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 7<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smtd202301277-fig-0007&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmtd.202301277" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a,b) The XRD curves of NVPF@rGO/CNT at different potential stages. c) Volume variation for NVPF@rGO/CNT and other advanced SIB cathode materials.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>In summary, the NVPF@rGO/CNT exhibits ultrahigh rate performance as well as excellent cycling stability without the addition of conductive additives. The superiorities of the NVPF@rGO/CNT structure have been investigated, and its excellent electrochemical property is benefited by the following aspects: 1) The 3D conductive network composed of rGO and CNT accelerates electron transport and enhances the conductivity of the NVPF@rGO/CNT electrode. 2) The larger cell volume and zero-strain characteristics of the NVPF@rGO/CNT are beneficial for improving cycling stability and accelerating Na<sup>+</sup> ions diffusion kinetic. Additionally, the removal of conductive additives is advantageous for reducing battery cost, increasing the proportion of active materials in the electrode, and enhancing energy density.</p>
         
         <p>Taking into account that in practical applications, the working temperature of batteries varies significantly due to geographic environments, which greatly impacts their electrochemical performance. To investigate electrode practicality and environmental tolerance, measured the electrochemical performance of all samples at different temperatures (−40, −20, 0, and 50). At a high temperature (50&nbsp;°C), the NVPF@rGO/CNT cathode displays a reversible capacity of 115 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> when charge/discharge at 1 C (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#smtd202301277-fig-0008">8a</a>), slightly lower than that at 25&nbsp;°C (120.6 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>). However, at an ultrahigh rate of 60 C, the NVPF@rGO/CNT electrode exhibits a favorable reversible capacity of 108.1 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, which is higher than that at 25&nbsp;°C (101 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>). This is owing to the quickening diffusion rate of Na<sup>+</sup> in electrolyte and electrode material as the temperature rises, thereby improving rate performance. This indicates that electrode material has good thermal stability and rapid insertion/extraction of Na<sup>+</sup> at high temperatures does not cause material structure collapse. Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7</a> (Supporting Information) shows the specific capacity of NVPF@rGO/CNT, NVPF@rGO, and NVPF electrodes at all rates. The NVPF@rGO/CNT cathode exhibits the highest reversible capacity. At −20&nbsp;°C, the NVPF@rGO/CNT electrode still exhibits good rate performance (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smtd202301277-fig-0008">8b</a>), with a satisfactory capacity of 80.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 5 C, significantly higher than NVPF@rGO (69.5 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>) and NVPF (21.1 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>). At −40&nbsp;°C, NVPF@rGO/CNT electrode has an acceptable discharge capacity of 106.7 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.2 C (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S14b</a>, Supporting Information). However, when the current reaches 5 C, the capacity experiences severe decay due to the temperature being close to the freezing point of the electrolyte, which severely hinders the migration of Na<sup>+</sup> in the electrolyte.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smtd202301277-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smtd202301277-bib-0028_R_d41595900e1636" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Energy Environ. Sci. Chem. Soc. Rev.">28</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The data of rate capability at different temperatures and the GCD curves are presented in Tables <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8–S10</a> and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15</a> (Supporting Information). For greater clarity, a bar chart comparison of discharge capacities across a wide temperature range (50, 25, 0, −20, and −40&nbsp;°C) at 1 C is presented in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smtd202301277-fig-0008">8c–e</a>. NVPF@rGO/CNT electrode displays a reversible capacity of 96.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at −40°C, equivalent to 80.3% of its discharge capacity at 25°C, while NVPF@rGO and NVPF electrodes show only 70.5% (81.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>) and 39.3% (34 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>), respectively. It is worth noting that the rate capability and reversible capacity of the NVPF@rGO/CNT electrode significantly exceed those of other recently reported Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>F<sub>3</sub> and Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> electrodes in a wide temperature range (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smtd202301277-fig-0008">8f</a>; Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smtd202301277-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smtd202301277-bib-0012_R_d41595900e1683" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - Adv. Energy Mater.">12</a>, <a href="#smtd202301277-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smtd202301277-bib-0022_R_d41595900e1683" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - Energy Storage Mater. InfoMat J. Energy Chem. Chem. Eng. J. Adv. Mater.">22</a>, <a href="#smtd202301277-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smtd202301277-bib-0029_R_d41595900e1683" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Mater. Today Chem. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces Adv. Energy Mater. J. Am. Chem. Soc. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">29</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The cycling performances of the NVPF@rGO/CNT cathode at low temperatures were evaluated at 1 C (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smtd202301277-fig-0008">8g</a>). After 200 cycles at 0&nbsp;°C, the NVPF@rGO/CNT cathode still maintained a discharge capacity of 106.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, equivalent to 97.4% of its initial capacity. The NVPF@rGO and NVPF electrodes maintained discharging capacities of 99.7 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> (96.8%) and 57.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> (94.4%), respectively. The kinetic differences of different electrodes at low temperatures (−40&nbsp;°C) were analyzed by the GITT test. GITT curves of the NVPF@rGO/CNT, NVPF@rGO, and NVPF at −40&nbsp;°C are portrayed in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16a–c</a>, (Supporting Information). Based on the GITT profiles, the D<sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> values are calculated and summarized in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16d–f</a>, (Supporting Information). Typically, the D<sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> value of NVPF@rGO/CNT ranges from 5&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−11</sup> to 2&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−10</sup>, which is higher than that of NVPF@rGO (from 3&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−11</sup> to 1.3&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−10</sup>) and NVPF (from 3&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−11</sup> to 1.2&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−10</sup>), show faster Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics in NVPF@rGO/CNT at −40&nbsp;°C. The GITT results showed that NVPF@rGO/CNT also has the advantage of Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics at low temperatures. All data indicate that the NVPF@rGO/@CNT electrode has the best electrochemical performance, demonstrating its good environmental adaptability.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="smtd202301277-fig-0008"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/9be7670b-ac05-46d6-8aa1-bf4e9d8296e2/smtd202301277-fig-0008-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/9be7670b-ac05-46d6-8aa1-bf4e9d8296e2/smtd202301277-fig-0008-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/5a1d58e3-de93-488f-95e7-11084955fda0/smtd202301277-fig-0008-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/9be7670b-ac05-46d6-8aa1-bf4e9d8296e2/smtd202301277-fig-0008-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 8<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smtd202301277-fig-0008&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmtd.202301277" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Electrochemical performance over a wide temperature range. a) Rate performance at 50&nbsp;°C, b) rate performance at −20&nbsp;°C, c) discharge capacity and capacity retention at various temperatures of NVPF@rGO/CNT, d) discharge capacity and capacity retention at various temperatures of NVPF@rGO, e) discharge capacity and capacity retention at various temperatures of NVPF, f) Ragone plot at different temperatures, g) Cycle performance at 1 C at 0&nbsp;°C.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>Taking into account the comprehensive discussions above, the superiority of NVPF@rGO/CNT electrodes is reflected in the following aspects: 1) The NVPF@rGO/CNT exhibits ultrahigh rate performance as well as excellent cycling stability without the addition of conductive additives. Removing conductive agents is advantageous for reducing battery costs, increasing the proportion of active materials in electrodes, and enhancing the energy density of electrodes. 2) The 3D conductive network composed of rGO and CNT accelerates electron transport and enhances the conductivity of the NVPF@rGO/CNT electrode. 3) The larger crystal volume of NVPF@rGO/CNT can accelerate the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics, thereby enhancing the rate performance. 4) The zero-strain characteristics of the NVPF are beneficial for improving cycling stability. 5) NVPF@rGO/CNT electrodes exhibit outstanding electrochemical performance within a temperature range of −40 to 50&nbsp;°C, indicating their good wide temperature adaptability.</p>
         
         <p>To further expound the usability of the NVPF@rGO/CNT cathode, a full battery was assembled with an HC anode. Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17</a> (Supporting Information) illustrates the rate capability of the HC anode. The specific capacity is 318, 259, 244, 227, and 203&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively, at rates of 0.1, 0.5, 1, 2, and 5 A g<sup>−1</sup>. <b>Figure</b> <a href="#smtd202301277-fig-0009">9a</a> displays the GCD curves of the NVPF@rGO/CNT cathode (10 C) and HC anode (2 A g<sup>−1</sup>) in the half cell, respectively. The electrochemical performance of the full battery was measured in the potential scope of 2 to 4.3&nbsp;V, and when cycled at 0.2 C, the Initial Coulombic Efficiency (ICE) was calculated as 65%. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smtd202301277-fig-0009">9b–d</a> exhibits the rate capability of the sodium ion full battery. The GCD curves exhibit good symmetry, indicating that the full cell has good electrochemical reversibility. Satisfactory reversible capacities of 105.2, 106, 104.5, 102, 97.6, 92.9, 89.5, and 86.6 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> are achieved at rates of 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, 5, 10, 15, and 20 C, respectively (based on the cathode mass). This sodium-ion full cell displayed an attractive energy density of 242.7&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> and power density of 60.7&nbsp;W kg<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smtd202301277-fig-0009">9c</a>, according to the add-up mass of cathode and anode active materials). Especially, as the power density reaches 5591&nbsp;W kg<sup>−1</sup>, a high energy density of 189.5&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> can still be left. The cycling stability of the sodium-ion full cell was measured under a current density of 1 C, and even after 200 cycles, it still maintained a favorable capacity retention of 94.5%. Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18</a> (Supporting Information) shows the EIS changes of an assembled full cell before the cycle test and after 10 cycles. The EIS results showed that the R<sub>ct</sub> was ≈6.2 Ω before cycling, and slightly increased to 6.6 Ω after the first cycle, and the slope in the low-frequency region decreased slightly, indicating a slight decrease in sodium ion diffusion rate. This is due to the formation of SEI during the first cycle. It is important to note that the EIS remained unchanged during subsequent cycles, indicating outstanding electrochemical stability of the full cell. The above excellent electrochemical performance of this full cell demonstrates the promising potential of NVPF@rGO/CNT as SIB cathode for practical applications.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="smtd202301277-fig-0009"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/1c0cb6a3-d677-43f2-a052-3b77979b729a/smtd202301277-fig-0009-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/1c0cb6a3-d677-43f2-a052-3b77979b729a/smtd202301277-fig-0009-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/62a3e631-42c0-4aaf-b87e-70233ec4fa18/smtd202301277-fig-0009-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/1c0cb6a3-d677-43f2-a052-3b77979b729a/smtd202301277-fig-0009-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 9<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smtd202301277-fig-0009&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmtd.202301277" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Electrochemical performances of full cell based on HC anode and NVPF@rGO@CNT cathode. a) GCD curves of NVPF@rGO@CNT cathode and HC anode, b) GCD curves at various current density, c) Ragone plots, d) rate performances, and e) cycle performance at 1&nbsp;C.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
      </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="smtd202301277-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="smtd202301277-sec-0030-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, we have successfully synthesized zero-strain NVPF@rGO/CNT as SIB cathodes. The NVPF@rGO/CNT exhibits ultrahigh rate performance (101 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 60 C), and superior cycling stability (capacity retention of 88.4% at 10 C after 6000 cycles) even without the addition of a conductive agent. The CV, GITT, and EIS tests further demonstrate the fast electrochemical dynamics of the NVPF@rGO/CNT cathode. Ex situ XRD reveals the zero-strain characteristic (volume variation of 0.4 %) of NVPF@rGO/CNT, which is responsible for its decent cyclability. Furthermore, the NVPF@rGO/CNT electrode displays prominent wide-temperature tolerance within a temperature range of 90&nbsp;°C (50 to −40&nbsp;°C) and maintains a superb reversible capacity of 96.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at −40&nbsp;°C. The full cell assembled by NVPF@rGO/CNT cathode and hard carbon anode enables a high energy density of 242.7&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> based on the total mass of the cathode and anode. Our study provides a reference for the reasonable design of high-rate and wide-temperature adaptive SIB cathode materials.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="smtd202301277-sec-0040">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="smtd202301277-sec-0040-title">4 Experimental Section</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smtd202301277-sec-0050">
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smtd202301277-sec-0060">
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smtd202301277-sec-0070">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smtd202301277-sec-0070-title"> Synthesis of NVPF Precursor</h4>
                  
                  <p>The NVPF precursor was prepared using the microwave-assisted hydrothermal technique. First, 1.4&nbsp;mmol vanadium (III) acetylacetonate [V-(acac)<sub>2</sub>] was dispersed into absolute alcohol (32&nbsp;mL) and stirred for 0.5&nbsp;h to create solution A. Next, NaF (2.1&nbsp;mmol) and NH<sub>4</sub>H<sub>2</sub>PO<sub>4</sub> (2.1&nbsp;mmol) were dispersed in a stoichiometric ratio into deionized (DI) water (45&nbsp;mL) and stirred 0.5&nbsp;h to mark as mixture B. Lastly, solution A was added to mixture B. The blended solution was moved to an autoclave and exposed to microwave-assisted hydrothermal reaction at 130&nbsp;°C for 1&nbsp;h. The resulting powder was centrifuged and washed three times with DI water. Finally, the NVPF precursor was obtained by freezing drying.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smtd202301277-sec-0080">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smtd202301277-sec-0080-title"> Synthesis of NVPF</h4>
                  
                  <p>The resulting NVPF precursor was sintered at 600&nbsp;°C for 7&nbsp;h in N<sub>2</sub> environment to produce NVPF.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smtd202301277-sec-0090">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smtd202301277-sec-0090-title"> Synthesis of NVPF@rGO/CNT</h4>
                  
                  <p>Initially, the prepared NVPF precursor (450&nbsp;mg), carbon nanotube (CNT) (7&nbsp;mg), and GO suspension (2&nbsp;mg mL<sup>−1</sup>, 7&nbsp;mL) were uniformly dispersed into glycol (15&nbsp;mL) using ultrasonic stirring for 2&nbsp;h to produce a uniformly a mixed solution. The commixture solution was then moved to an autoclave and subjected to a solvothermal reaction for 24&nbsp;h at 200&nbsp;°C in order to produce the NVPF precursor@GO/CNT gel. The resulting gel was centrifuged and washed three times with DI before being freeze-dried to obtain the NVPF precursor@GO@CNT, which was then calcined at 600&nbsp;°C for 7&nbsp;h in an N<sub>2</sub> environment.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smtd202301277-sec-0100">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smtd202301277-sec-0100-title"> Synthesis of NVPF@rGO</h4>
                  
                  <p>The synthesis of NVPF@rGO was carried out using the same method as NVPF@rGO/CNT, with the exception that CNT was not added to NVPF@rGO and instead, a higher amount of GO was incorporated (2&nbsp;mg mL<sup>−1</sup>,10&nbsp;mL).</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smtd202301277-sec-0110">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smtd202301277-sec-0110-title"> Synthesis of NVPF@rGO-600&nbsp;°C</h4>
                  
                  <p>The method of synthesizing NVPF@rGO-600&nbsp;°C using microwave-assisted hydrothermal synthesis had been reported in the previous research.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smtd202301277-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smtd202301277-bib-0021_R_d41595900e1898" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">21</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> First, 0.7&nbsp;mmol V-(acac)<sub>2</sub> was dissolved in 24&nbsp;mL absolute alcohol and stirred for 0.5&nbsp;h, resulting in a solution referred to as A. Then 1.05&nbsp;mmol NH<sub>4</sub>H<sub>2</sub>PO<sub>4</sub>, 1.05&nbsp;mmol NaF and rGO solution (2&nbsp;mg mL<sup>−1</sup>, 18&nbsp;mL) was dissolved into DI water (30&nbsp;mL) and stirred for 0.5&nbsp;h to form a mixture referred to as B. Subsequently, mixture B was added to solution A, and the mixed solution was placed in an autoclave and subjected to microwave-assisted hydrothermal reaction at 130&nbsp;°C for 1&nbsp;h. The produce powder was centrifuged and washed three times with DI water. Finally, the precursor was obtained by freeze-drying, which was then calcined at 600°C for 7&nbsp;h in an N<sub>2</sub> environment.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smtd202301277-sec-0120">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smtd202301277-sec-0120-title"> Materials Characterization</h4>
                  
                  <p>Scanning electron microscopy (SEM, Apreo 2S HiVac) and transmission electron microscopy (TEM, Talos F200S) were used to study the morphology of samples. Crystallography of all samples was characterized using X-ray diffractometry (XRD, D/MAX-Ultima IV) in the 2<i>θ</i> range of 5° to 85° (<i>λ</i> = 0.15406&nbsp;nm). The FullProf program was used for the Rietveld refinement method to refine the powder patterns. The Raman spectra of the prepared samples were measured using the Raman spectrometer (LabRAM HR Evolution) with a 532&nbsp;nm light source. X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS, Escalab 250Xi) was utilized to analyze the surface species and chemical state of the samples. A thermogravimetric-differential thermal analysis (TG-DTA) was conducted using an STA 449C Netzsch thermal analyzer with a heating rate of 5&nbsp;°C min<sup>−1</sup> up to 800&nbsp;°C under an air atmosphere. The Brunauer–Emmett–Teller (BET) specific surface area was studied by nitrogen adsorption–desorption (3H-2000PS1).</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smtd202301277-sec-0130">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smtd202301277-sec-0130-title"> Electrode Preparation and Electrochemical Measurements</h4>
                  
                  <p>The samples were assembled into 2032 coin-type cells in order to test their electrochemical properties. The NVPF@rGO/CNT (or NVPF@rGO) electrode was made by mixing 90 wt.% NVPF@rGO/CNT (or NVPF@rGO) sample with 10 wt.% polyvinylidene fluoride (PVDF) without any conductive additives and uniformly dispersing it in <i>N</i>-methyl-2-pyrrolidone (NMP). The resulting slurry was then coated onto a carbon-coated Al foil. In comparison, the pure NVPF electrode was also fabricated using an electrode containing 10 wt.% PVDF, 10 wt.% conductive carbon black (CB), and 80 wt.% NVPF powder. After evaporating the NMP using the vacuum drying oven at 60&nbsp;°C for 12 h to produce electrode. The reference electrode and counter electrode were made of sodium metal foil, and the electrolyte used in the experiment was a commercially available 1&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span> NaPF<sub>6</sub> in diglyme, with a glass fiber membrane used as a separator. The hard carbon (HC) anode was assembled by mixing 70 wt.% HC with 10 wt.% carboxymethylcellulose sodium (CMC) and 20 wt.% CB in deionized water, following the same assembly process as the cathode. The loading of active materials in the NVPF@rGO/CNT cathode and HC anode during assembly of the full cell was ≈2 and ≈1&nbsp;mg cm<sup>−2</sup>, respectively.</p>
                  
                  <p>The CV curves and EIS measurements were undertaken on an electrochemical workstation (CHI760E, Shanghai, China). The rate capability, cycling performances, and GITT were measured on a battery test device (BTS7.6.0, Neware battery-test instrument). Electrochemical performances of electrodes at different temperatures were tested at a battery test device (BTS7.6.0, Neware battery-test instrument) in a temperature-controllable test chamber (Neware MGDW-150-40).</p>
                  </section>
               </section>
            </section>
         </section>

                  <li data-bib-id="smtd202301277-bib-0003"><span class="bullet">3</span>a) <span class="author">C. Vaalma</span>, <span class="author">D. Buchholz</span>, <span class="author">M.
